<trips-parser-output parser-build-date="2018-11-15T16:18:53-0600" system="DRUM" extsformat="svg" tagsformat="hidden" treecontents="phrase" treeformat="LinGO" lfformat="svg" rule-sets="aesop,anon,lg,sri,test,test1,testactivate,ttt,wdebeaum" input="T-cells are entirely quiescent in the absence of antigen signals, but are shifted rapidly into a state of activation following TCR ligation. Inappropriate control of this activation can lead to autoimmune disease, and therefore negative feedback loops are an inherent feature of T-cell biology. Recent data show that Notch signals block Akt activation in peripheral CD4+ T-cells [13]. Indeed we also observe that in primary human CD4+ T-cells recombinant Delta1-IgG4 fusion protein, or Notch-IC expression, blocks TCR-mediated phosphorylation of Akt and GSK3β (GM, BC, unpublished data). Although Akt activation is essential for production of cytokines such as IL2 and IFNγ by T-cells [24], constitutive activity is associated with cellular transformation [25], and therefore the existence of a negative feedback loop to limit antigen-dependent Akt activation would appear rational. We have shown that co-incident Notch signals are enhanced upon TCR activation, and we hypothesise that by inhibiting Akt activity, enhanced Notch signalling may constitute a negative feedback control impacting upon peripheral T-cell activation.">

Pruning agenda with beam width 50</debug><ekb complete="true" id="TEXT00004_IO-118350" timestamp="20190628T135226"><input type="text"><paragraphs><paragraph file="/Users/wbeaumont/drum/etc/Data/WP/TEXT00004_IO-118350" id="paragraph3">T-cells are entirely quiescent in the absence of antigen signals, but are shifted rapidly into a state of activation following TCR ligation. Inappropriate control of this activation can lead to autoimmune disease, and therefore negative feedback loops are an inherent feature of T-cell biology. Recent data show that Notch signals block Akt activation in peripheral CD4+ T-cells [13]. Indeed we also observe that in primary human CD4+ T-cells recombinant Delta1-IgG4 fusion protein, or Notch-IC expression, blocks TCR-mediated phosphorylation of Akt and GSK3β (GM, BC, unpublished data). Although Akt activation is essential for production of cytokines such as IL2 and IFNγ by T-cells [24], constitutive activity is associated with cellular transformation [25], and therefore the existence of a negative feedback loop to limit antigen-dependent Akt activation would appear rational. We have shown that co-incident Notch signals are enhanced upon TCR activation, and we hypothesise that by inhibiting Akt activity, enhanced Notch signalling may constitute a negative feedback control impacting upon peripheral T-cell activation.
